<div id="review_44683733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44683733" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44683733?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780743211383" href="/book/show/441240.Dreamcatcher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44683733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14241968173966692462">Stephen King is truly gifted. In this book, he takes a cheesy overdone concept (alien/body snatchers) and makes it work.<br/><br/>This isn't the best King book, but it is far from being his worst. I didn't have hugely high expectations other than being able to chuckle everytime somebody said "shit weasels", but I was pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/>I saw the movie a few times, and while I enjoyed it, this wasn't something that should have won any Oscars. That lowered my expectations some.<br/><br/>I'm not a huge fan of alien-</span>
  <span id="freeText14241968173966692462" style="display:none">Stephen King is truly gifted. In this book, he takes a cheesy overdone concept (alien/body snatchers) and makes it work.<br /><br />This isn't the best King book, but it is far from being his worst. I didn't have hugely high expectations other than being able to chuckle everytime somebody said "shit weasels", but I was pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />I saw the movie a few times, and while I enjoyed it, this wasn't something that should have won any Oscars. That lowered my expectations some.<br /><br />I'm not a huge fan of alien-based science fiction. It's been overdone as I've said before, and hasn't been cool since Duchovny/Anderson starred on X-Files together. So again, my expectations were lowered.<br /><br />The shit-weasels also lowered my expectations. Sure, it's funny to say it, and they provide many opportunities for juvenile laughter, but really? Who wants to read about a monster who incubates in a person's intestines and exits through said person's ass? It might work in a Jay and Silent Bob movie, but this is literature. <br /><br />Now, despite all my misgivings, which compiled to keep me from reading this book for the first eight years of its existence, I wanted to knock it out and work towards my goal of completing Stephen King's library.<br /><br />I loved this book! The characters are so well drawn up. Pete, Henry, Jonesy, and Beaver. Plus Duddits, their "dreamcatcher", who they meet and rescue as boys, and who changes their lives forever. I love how we're thrown into the action early on as they're adults, then get glimpses into their childhood days which piece the story together. <br /><br />It's really very layered and complex. The aliens themselves, not so much, though they do tie in to the structure pretty well through the interaction of Jonesy with "Mr. Gray." But the strength of this book is the principal five characters that grew up in Derry together and must now face this menace that threatens humankind.<br /><br />Also, I loved Kurtz! The perfect black-ops nutjob colonel. Crazy as a freakin' loon. This man might have been a military cousin to Jim Rennie from Under the Dome.<br /><br />Bravo, Mr. King, for weaving together this dreamcatcher. One of the more memorable novel of the early 21st Century. <br /><br />And just so I can say it one more time: shit weasels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14241968173966692462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2549071976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2549071976" />
    <a title="SAM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57392386-sam"><img alt="SAM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556638019p2/57392386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2549071976?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SAM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SAM" href="/user/show/57392386-sam">SAM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780340770726" href="/book/show/155576.Dreamcatcher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2549071976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8182453153726065176">Although Stephen King novels/short stories are currently experiencing a big screen revival some of the earlier efforts are still pretty poor. The likes of Thinner, The Stand and the Nightmares & Dreamscapes TV series did not transfer well. I made the mistake of watching the film version of Dreamcatcher before reading the novel and for years, whilst browsing the shelves of second hand book stores and charity shops, my eyes would register the presence of Dreamcatcher but i never considered picking</span>
  <span id="freeText8182453153726065176" style="display:none">Although Stephen King novels/short stories are currently experiencing a big screen revival some of the earlier efforts are still pretty poor. The likes of Thinner, The Stand and the Nightmares &amp; Dreamscapes TV series did not transfer well. I made the mistake of watching the film version of Dreamcatcher before reading the novel and for years, whilst browsing the shelves of second hand book stores and charity shops, my eyes would register the presence of Dreamcatcher but i never considered picking it up. My immediate reaction was ‘My god the film was awful!’. But now i’m running out of Kings to read I gave it a chance and i’m so glad i did.<br /><br />The plot is kind of familiar in the world of Stephen King stories. Four childhood friends with varying degrees of telekinesis, all of them slightly damaged by real life in some way, meet up for what proves to be their final yearly hunting trip. A confused stranger, looking deathly ill, enters the camp spouting nonsense about lights in the sky and what follows is an excellent Alien Invasion story done in the classic Stephen King style.<br /><br />There is a slight similarity to IT in that the four friends are linked by an heroic act from their childhood and are required to retell and flashback to it years later but i preferred this to IT. For me, IT was way too long, monotonous in places and such a chore to finish. Dreamcatcher is half the size, better written and has way more action as there is very little messing around and build up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8182453153726065176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_333977393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333977393" />
    <a title="Jonathan Briggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6903743-jonathan-briggs"><img alt="Jonathan Briggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501205790p2/6903743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333977393?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Briggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Briggs" href="/user/show/6903743-jonathan-briggs">Jonathan Briggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780743436274" href="/book/show/228124.Dreamcatcher">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333977393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10898140745333520532">Ree-damn-diculous. Aliens bursting from butts. Frothing military maniacs. A Magic Retard (Stephen King's go-to character when the Magic Negro is busy). Ludicrous, labored faux-blue-collar dialogue. And farts. Constant, neverending, rancid, moist farts. This may be the stupidest book King has ever written, and that's saying something. And yet ... I kept thinking he was doing it on purpose, that he wrote this as a horror comedy, a la "Slither." King has written some godawful garbage in his career,</span>
  <span id="freeText10898140745333520532" style="display:none">Ree-damn-diculous. Aliens bursting from butts. Frothing military maniacs. A Magic Retard (Stephen King's go-to character when the Magic Negro is busy). Ludicrous, labored faux-blue-collar dialogue. And farts. Constant, neverending, rancid, moist farts. This may be the stupidest book King has ever written, and that's saying something. And yet ... I kept thinking he was doing it on purpose, that he wrote this as a horror comedy, a la "Slither." King has written some godawful garbage in his career, but none of it was near this entertaining. "Dreamcatcher" is bad, but it's hilariously bad. This is a book in which bacon saves the planet (OK, that's not such a stretch). I spent my train commutes to work and back quaking with laughter while reading this. It's FUN! "Insomnia" wasn't fun. It just sucked. "Desperation" just sucked. "Dreamcatcher" is a different beastie altogether: “You could only compare it to farts because there was nothing else even close.” Thank you, Stephen King, thank you for showing those National Book Award snobs the way. I can't, in good conscience, give this any more than three stars. It's a wretched novel, and King should be ashamed of himself for writing it. As ashamed as I am for enjoying it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10898140745333520532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer593889615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15608845136093623780">Aliens attack Maine, a homicidal poop is trapped in a toilet, and one of the characters uses his shoe as a telephone. That's about all I remember from "Dreamcatcher", not one of Stephen King's finest, I daresay. Still, I remember enjoying it, years ago when I first read it. I vaguely recall the mediocre movie, too, which featured a stellar cast including Morgan Freeman, Thomas Jane, Timothy Oliphant, and Tom Sizemore. One of the weirdest alien invasion stories I've ever read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1205474-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564000674p2/1205474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23510781?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/1205474-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Science fiction fans, thiller fans, Stephen King fans, alien invasion fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer23510781&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23510781" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12603631497324377036">	I have been a fan of Stephen King since my brother Scott recommended the Dark Tower series to me. My wife knows to check the thrift stores that she frequents for King novels, and “Dreamcatcher” was one that she found. I didn’t know anything about the story, but sat down to begin reading a week and a half ago or so.<br/>	The story is about an alien invasion, and that was enough to get my interest. Although there are many aspects involved, including four friends caught in the middle of it, the militar</span>
  <span id="freeText12603631497324377036" style="display:none">	I have been a fan of Stephen King since my brother Scott recommended the Dark Tower series to me. My wife knows to check the thrift stores that she frequents for King novels, and “Dreamcatcher” was one that she found. I didn’t know anything about the story, but sat down to begin reading a week and a half ago or so.<br />	The story is about an alien invasion, and that was enough to get my interest. Although there are many aspects involved, including four friends caught in the middle of it, the military cleanup, conflicts between the soldiers and their questionable orders, and many memories and flashbacks, the real story is about a Down syndrome man named Duddits who changes everything. This is the first King novel that came close to bringing me to tears, and his ability to make his reader really like and care about poor Duddits is excellent. I don’t think I will ever look at a person who has Down syndrome the same way again.<br /><br />3.75	Characters<br />	Presenting realistic, interesting characters is one of King’s strong suits, and he does not fail here. The four friends, Owen Underhill, and the cast they encounter in their adventures are all complex and involving. Extra points go for Kurtz, the insane military leader in charge of the government cleanup. He always kept me on my toes. Duddits was also a great character that I cared about, and is central to everything.<br /><br />3.5	Pace<br />	King is a master of suspense, but sometimes it is aggravating. He spends a lot of time establishing background and building things up before he lets loose. It’s a good pace, but there were parts that almost bored me. The last few hundred pages had me on the edge of my seat though.<br /><br />3	Story<br />	The alien invasion in the novel is original, but the concept of four childhood friends with a strange gift being caught in the middle of it an old friend to the author. I thought the most engaging parts of the story were about the military cleanup. I also thought that Duddits was a brilliant part of the story, and King does a good job of getting his reader to care for him.<br />	I have to dock the story points because of the lack of research by the author and his editors. Among other mistakes that I consider elementary, he refers to a “cook’s third” in an Army unit (that sounds like a Navy designation), and also says that an H&amp;K Mp5 fires 5.56mm ammunition when it fires 9mm. They’re small details, but the mistakes took my attention away from the story and ruined the suspension of disbelief for moments at a time.<br /><br />2.5	Dialogue<br />	King is very good at dialogue, but there were a few parts that felt weak or too wordy/preachy. There were a few times when Henry, and even crazy Kurtz who had a reason to talk crazy, stopped being realistic.<br /><br />5	Style/Technical<br />	There is no doubt in my mind that this book is an excellent example of a seasoned, veteran author using the tools of his trade to produce a superior novel. Most of my Stephen King material has been his earlier works, and he has grown and learned a lot in the years. His shifting viewpoints, flashbacks, changes of scenery, presentation of dreams, and integrating everything into the narrative is nothing short of amazing.<br /><br />3.6	Overall<br />	“Dreamcatcher” is a good alien invasion story, but a better examination of the human condition than most escapist fiction. Jonesy’s battle against the alien entity possessing his body, Kurtz’s mad logic, and everything about Duddits are amazing examples of fiction writing. My only real complaint would be a degree of predictability after the midway point.<br />	At the same time, I think the novel also gives some insight into Stephen King’s mindset. He clearly is not familiar with things of a military nature in any way, and apparently neither are his editors. This tells me that he doesn’t really understand the people who volunteer to serve and put on those uniforms. As a result, most of his soldier characters come across as raving lunatics. It serves his story, but it’s an example of how he does not know that part of society and assigns unfair stereotypes to them.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12603631497324377036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_29333874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29333874" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29333874?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29333874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4364542995069676079">I've put off writing a review because Becky wrote the review to end all reviews and said it all! It's my resolution to review <b>all</b> the books I read this year so I have to make the attempt. Here goes...<br/><br/>I read this the week it first came out in 2001 because I always read his books as soon as they come out. At breakneck speed more often than not. I tend to re-read and savor the books later, but the first reading is like a "fix" I have been Jonesing for, so taking my time is not really an option. I w</span>
  <span id="freeText4364542995069676079" style="display:none">I've put off writing a review because Becky wrote the review to end all reviews and said it all! It's my resolution to review <b>all</b> the books I read this year so I have to make the attempt. Here goes...<br /><br />I read this the week it first came out in 2001 because I always read his books as soon as they come out. At breakneck speed more often than not. I tend to re-read and savor the books later, but the first reading is like a "fix" I have been Jonesing for, so taking my time is not really an option. I was especially happy to get this particular fix because I had been so devastated when King had his accident. This book was proof he had not left us.<br /><br />This is one of the few I never went back to re-read. Until now. I couldn't even think of this book without flenching my glutes, so my aversion was understandable. This time around I wonder what took me so long! Yes, I giggled through the horrendous gas and "birthing" of the poop weasels, but once I got over that I really enjoyed this densely layered book.<br /><br />I always love when King writes about aliens. In Dreamcatcher, aliens have been present on our world for a long time. The military is very aware of their probes and visits. The book starts with 4 childhood friends, all grown up now, meeting for their annual hunting trip in a cabin dead center of ground zero. Needless to say, with them being King characters, they all carry a lot of emotional baggage. The guys share a LOT of history that King peels like an onion in flashbacks thoughout the story.<br /><br /> At the onset of a huge storm, the aliens arrive, en masse, in thier ship. They are broadcasting, in highly recognizable human voices, English and French, "There is no infection here.". Has an ominous ring to it, huh? Fortunately they land in the woods in the middle of just about nowhere. Not quite so fortunate is the fact that it's hunting season. The military swoops in to contain the "virus" the aliens have introduced, (guess they were lying about the "no infection" part) and begin these efforts by rounding up all the hunters and corralling them. These particular aliens seem intent only on survival. They aren't out to wipe out mankind...unless humans interfere with said survival, that is.<br /><br />In addition to the "grey boys" we've come to expect of aliens, there is a red, mosslike growth of a virus humans can become infected with AND a small creature, the aforementioned poop weasels that incubate in the human digestive track, eventually eating thier way out. Our four hunting friends end with the fate of the world, literally, in their hands with the help of thier very, very special fifth friend from childhood.<br /><br />One of the effects of close proximity to the aliens is ESP. Our friends have shared a bit of a mental bond and heightened perception since childhood, and this just ups their mental abilities to the nth. It may sound cool to be able to read your neighbors, family and friends minds, but if you carry that thought to the final conclusion...it's not! It causes havoc, distrust, hate, fear and above all panic. I felt panic was the tone of this book. It takes place over the course of just 2 days, and beginning to end is constant action at breakneck speed. It is NOT a slow boil.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4364542995069676079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_228720812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228720812" />
    <a title="Jessika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166992-jessika"><img alt="Jessika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547989302p2/1166992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228720812?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessika" href="/user/show/1166992-jessika">Jessika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780743436274" href="/book/show/228124.Dreamcatcher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166992-jessika?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228720812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5461729835171591068">I was pretty wary when I started this book. I read The Tommyknockers a few years back, and I felt kinda "meh" about it. I've never been big on "alien" stories. I've heard some people describe Dreamcatcher as a blend between The Tommyknockers and IT, and now having finished, I have to say that's a pretty accurate description. I was also a little nervous because I've heard people say that Stephen King's newer stuff just isn't up to par with his older classics like IT or The Shining. <br/><br/>I shouldn't ha</span>
  <span id="freeText5461729835171591068" style="display:none">I was pretty wary when I started this book. I read The Tommyknockers a few years back, and I felt kinda "meh" about it. I've never been big on "alien" stories. I've heard some people describe Dreamcatcher as a blend between The Tommyknockers and IT, and now having finished, I have to say that's a pretty accurate description. I was also a little nervous because I've heard people say that Stephen King's newer stuff just isn't up to par with his older classics like IT or The Shining. <br /><br />I shouldn't have been so worried. This was an excellent read.<br /><br />I've said it before, and I'm sure I'll say it again: my favorite part of Stephen King's writing is his flawless character development. He has a knack for getting his readers truly invested in his characters, whether they are the main characters or even just minor characters around for a page or two. And his villains are always the nastiest that you can imagine. Kurtz gave me the creeps. Honestly, my favorite part of this book was reading about the friendship between Henry, Jonesy, Pete, Beaver and Duddits. I love that throughout all the action going on in the story's present-day, Stephen King takes the time to really make you understand what it is that makes their friendship so special. I know flashbacks aren't for everyone, but I liked how as the story went on, I got to see pieces of their past, never the whole thing all at once, which is what kept me reading. <br /><br />I can see how this book could be off-putting for some readers. Of all of his books that I've read, this one is pretty gross. I can handle gore, but I will warn squeamish readers that this is one you'll probably want to avoid. <br /><br />This book is pretty lengthy, as well. I found myself getting sucked into the story for hundreds of pages at a time, though. With any book of this length, there are bound to be faster parts and slower parts. But even through the slower parts, I found myself wondering what was going to happen to the characters and what the fate of the human race was going to be. And the last hundred pages? I felt myself getting stressed out because I HAD to know what was going to happen and I felt like I couldn't read fast enough to get there. <br /><br />Overall, it was very satisfying for me to sink into this Stephen King read, much like coming home to an old friend. I'm pretty sure I'm destined to enjoy everything he has ever written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5461729835171591068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CyPsBYGjpFL3heCugZrRXbK9L7MH/omDnGXURFyL3eka2YDS3LBoiOlmhwYjocJ+FGXIff+bh3096qr/L2w1dQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WTR2pvP62wJU0quD8DXuoY7tYqbhbau9eSnfd6yxS4FIzhpxrukX2EoxzCtSDv2CKDWFaBkIpUPYpqHM31ajHQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,326
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10537173846288065645">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText10537173846288065645" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10537173846288065645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
